  <script>
   function is_ie() {
				var ua = window.navigator.userAgent; //Check the userAgent property of the window.navigator object
				var msie = ua.indexOf('MSIE '); // IE 10 or older
				var trident = ua.indexOf('Trident/'); //IE 11

				return (msie > 0 || trident > 0);
			}

			function not_excluded_page() {
				return (window.location.href.indexOf("/unsupported-browser/") === - 1 && document.title.toLowerCase().indexOf('page not found') === - 1);
			}

			if (is_ie() && not_excluded_page()) {
				window.location = location.protocol + '//' + location.host + '/unsupported-browser/';
			}
  </script>

              </span>
             </button>
             <div aria-hidden="true" aria-labelledby="menu-item-1664" class="nav-primary__child nav-primary__child--depth-1" data-depth="1" data-js="child-menu" id="menu-item-child-1664">
              <div class="nav-primary__subsec nav-primary__subsec--top nav-primary__subsec--has-content nav-primary__subsec--depth-1">
               <div class="nav-primary__back nav-primary__back--depth-1">
                <button aria-controls="menu-item-child-1664" aria-expanded="true" aria-label="Return to main menu" class="nav-primary__back-action nav-primary__back-action--depth-1" data-js="trigger-menu-return" id="menu-item-back-1664" title="Return to main menu">
                 <span aria-hidden="true" class="nav-primary__back-action-icon icon icon-chevron-left">
                 </span>
                 In Focus
                </button>
               </div>
               <div class="nav-primary__subsec-header">
                <strong class="nav-primary__subsec-title">
                 <a class="nav-primary__subsec-title-link" data-attribute="whats-in-focus" href="/in-focus" rel="bookmark">
                  What's In Focus?
                  <span aria-hidden="true" class="icon icon-arrow-right">
                  </span>
                 </a>
                </strong>
                <span class="nav-primary__subsec-description">
                 Every week were highlighting subjects that have inspired the Harvard community to turn research and creativity into global action.
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
              <ol class="nav-primary__child-list nav-primary__child-list--depth-1">
               <li class="nav-primary__item nav-primary__item--depth-1 nav-primary__item--has-children nav-primary__item--sub-mob-vis-true">
                <button aria-controls="menu-item-child-11565" aria-expanded="false" class="nav-primary__action nav-primary__action--depth-1 nav-primary__action--has-children" data-attribute="poetry" data-depth="1" data-id="11565" data-id-parent="1664" data-js="trigger-child-menu" id="menu-item-11565" title="Toggle Sub-Menu">
                 <span class="nav-primary__action-text">
                  Poetry
                  <span aria-hidden="true" class="icon icon-chevron-right">
                  </span>
                 </span>
                </button>
                <div aria-hidden="true" aria-labelledby="menu-item-11565" class="nav-primary__child nav-primary__child--depth-2" data-depth="2" data-js="child-menu" id="menu-item-child-11565">
                 <div class="nav-primary__subsec nav-primary__subsec--top nav-primary__subsec--has-content nav-primary__subsec--depth-2">
                  <div class="nav-primary__back nav-primary__back--depth-2">
                   <button aria-controls="menu-item-child-11565" aria-expanded="true" aria-label="Return to main menu" class="nav-primary__back-action nav-primary__back-action--depth-2" data-js="trigger-menu-return" id="menu-item-back-11565" title="Return to main menu">
                    <span aria-hidden="true" class="nav-primary__back-action-icon icon icon-chevron-left">
                    </span>
                    In Focus
                   </button>
                  </div>
                  <div class="nav-primary__subsec-header">
                   <strong class="nav-primary__subsec-title">
                    Poetry
                   </strong>
                   <span class="nav-primary__subsec-description">
                    Harvard has been a home to poets and poetry scholars for centuries. Today, poetry flourishes here through scholarship and collaboration, in our vast archival collections, and in lively community readings and events.
                   </span>
                   <a class="nav-primary__subsec-cta" data-attribute="read-more" href="https://www.harvard.edu/in-focus/poetry/" rel="bookmark">
                    <span aria-hidden="true" class="icon icon-arrow-right">
                    </span>

    <header>
     <h1 class="screen-reader-text">
      Harvard University
     </h1>
    </header>
    <div class="h1 vertical-text">
     Poetry
    </div>
    <div class="the-follower" data-js="follower">
    </div>
    <div class="s-sink t-sink l-sink">
     <section class="c-block b-hero t-theme--light no-cta no-featured-story an-no-animate">
      <div class="b-hero__container l-container">
       <div class="b-hero__media b-hero__media-overlay--medium">
        <video aria-label="Background Video" autoplay="" class="b-hero__bg-video" loop="" muted="" playsinline="">
         <source src="https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/spaceloop.mp4" type="video/mp4">
         </source>
        </video>
       </div>
       <div class="b-hero__content">
        <header class="c-block__content-block c-block__header b-hero__content-container c-content-block c-content-block--layout-center">
         <h2 class="c-block__title b-hero__title b-hero__title--med c-content-block__title">
          Poetry and language are often at the heartbeat of movements for change.
          <br/>
          -Amanda Gorman
          <br/>
          <br/>
         </h2>
         <div class="c-content-block__content-wrap">
          <p class="c-content-block__cta">
           <a class="c-block__cta-link a-btn a-btn-primary a-btn--arrow-right c-content-block__cta-link" href="https://time.com/5933596/amanda-gorman-michelle-obama-interview/">
            <span class="a-btn__text">
             Michelle Obama, J.D. 88, interviews Amanda Gorman 20 in TIME
            </span>
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </header>
       </div>
       <div class="b-hero__meta-wrap">
        <div class="b-hero__meta">
         <button aria-label="Pause the video" class="a-btn-multimedia-secondary a-btn--icon-only b-hero__video-trigger" data-js="video-trigger">
          <span class="a-btn__text">
          </span>
         </button>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </section>
     <section class="c-block b-herosplit t-theme--light has-secondary-media an-no-animate">
      <div class="b-herosplit__container">
       <div class="b-herosplit__figure-secondary c-image--bg c-image--bg-split b-herosplit__figure-secondary--mobile b-herosplit__media-secondary-overlay c-image">
        <div aria-label="People sit reading and talking in a group with bookshelves behind them." class="b-herosplit__img-secondary c-image__image lazyload" data-bgset="https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/032312_Harvard_Poetry_017-1-1152x768.jpeg 1152w 768h" data-expand="200" data-sizes="(min-width: 1260px) 1260px, 100vw" role="img" style="background-image:url('https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/themes/core/assets/img/theme/shims/core-full.png');">
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="b-herosplit__media b-herosplit__media-overlay">
        <div class="b-herosplit__figure-secondary c-image--bg c-image--bg-split b-herosplit__figure-secondary--desktop c-image">
         <div aria-label="People sit reading and talking in a group with bookshelves behind them." class="b-herosplit__img-secondary c-image__image lazyload" data-bgset="https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/032312_Harvard_Poetry_017-1-1152x768.jpeg 1152w 768h" data-expand="200" data-sizes="(min-width: 1260px) 1260px, 100vw" role="img" style="background-image:url('https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/themes/core/assets/img/theme/shims/core-full.png');">
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="b-herosplit__figure c-image--bg c-image--bg-split c-image">
         <div aria-label="Students at table." class="b-herosplit__img c-image__image lazyload" data-bgset="https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/50953471651_86aadd3d53_k-1-1152x866.jpg 1152w 866h" data-expand="200" data-sizes="(min-width: 1260px) 1260px, 100vw" role="img" style="background-image:url('https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/themes/core/assets/img/theme/shims/core-full.png');">
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="b-herosplit__content">
        <header class="c-block__content-block c-block__header b-herosplit__content-container c-content-block c-content-block--layout-left">
         <h2 class="c-block__title b-herosplit__title c-content-block__title">
          Woodberry Poetry Room
         </h2>
         <div class="c-content-block__content-wrap">
          <div class="c-block__description b-herosplit__description t-sink s-sink c-content-block__content">
           <p>
            Nestled in Lamont Library in a room designed by renowned Finnish architect Alvar Aalto, youll find the Woodberry Poetry Room, a special collections reading room and audio-visual archive, and a lively literary center at Harvardfree and open to the public.
           </p>
           <p>
            The Poetry Room, a curatorial division of Houghton Library, features a circulating collection of 20th and 21st century poetry, over 150 literary magazines, and a landmark audio-visual collection featuring recordings from 1933 to the present day.
           </p>
           <p>
            With over 5,000 recordings on a range of media that span the 20th and 21st centuries, including phonodiscs, magnetic tape (reel to reel and cassette), CDs, DATs, and born digital, the collection is one of the largest and earliest poetry-specific sound archives in the United States.
           </p>
          </div>
          <p class="c-content-block__cta">
           <a class="c-block__cta-link a-btn a-btn-secondary a-btn--arrow-right c-content-block__cta-link" href="https://library.harvard.edu/libraries/poetryroom">
            <span class="a-btn__text">
             Visit the Woodberry Poetry Room at Harvard Library
            </span>
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </header>
       </div>
      </div>
     </section>
     <div class="c-block b-spacer t-theme--light all-screens reduce-spacing">
     </div>
     <div class="c-block b-spacer all-screens reduce-spacing">
     </div>
     <section class="c-block b-herosplit has-secondary-media content-left-align an-no-animate">
      <div class="b-herosplit__container">
       <div class="b-herosplit__figure-secondary c-image--bg c-image--bg-split b-herosplit__figure-secondary--mobile b-herosplit__media-secondary-overlay c-image">
        <div aria-label="Pressed leaves preserved on a piece of paper." class="b-herosplit__img-secondary c-image__image lazyload" data-bgset="https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/nrs.harvard.eduurn-3-FHCL.HOUGH-883158_n30.jpg 450w 680h" data-expand="200" data-sizes="(min-width: 1260px) 1260px, 100vw" role="img" style="background-image:url('https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/themes/core/assets/img/theme/shims/core-full.png');">
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="b-herosplit__media b-herosplit__media-overlay">
        <div class="b-herosplit__figure-secondary c-image--bg c-image--bg-split b-herosplit__figure-secondary--desktop c-image">
         <div aria-label="Pressed leaves preserved on a piece of paper." class="b-herosplit__img-secondary c-image__image lazyload" data-bgset="https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/nrs.harvard.eduurn-3-FHCL.HOUGH-883158_n30.jpg 450w 680h" data-expand="200" data-sizes="(min-width: 1260px) 1260px, 100vw" role="img" style="background-image:url('https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/themes/core/assets/img/theme/shims/core-full.png');">
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="b-herosplit__figure c-image--bg c-image--bg-split c-image">
         <div aria-label="Wooden chair at a small wooden desk." class="b-herosplit__img c-image__image lazyload" data-bgset="https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/101513_Dickinson_Archive_042-1152x768.jpeg 1152w 768h" data-expand="200" data-sizes="(min-width: 1260px) 1260px, 100vw" role="img" style="background-image:url('https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/themes/core/assets/img/theme/shims/core-full.png');">
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="b-herosplit__content">
        <header class="c-block__content-block c-block__header b-herosplit__content-container c-content-block c-content-block--layout-left">
         <h2 class="c-block__title b-herosplit__title c-content-block__title">
          Emily Dickinson Collection
         </h2>
         <div class="c-content-block__content-wrap">
          <div class="c-block__description b-herosplit__description t-sink s-sink c-content-block__content">
           <p>
            What kind of desk did Emily Dickinson sit at when she penned Hope is the Thing with Feathers? What did her handwriting look like? What sorts of herbs and flowers did the poet preserve in her fabled
            <a href="https://iiif.lib.harvard.edu/manifests/view/drs:4184689$1i">
             Herbarium
            </a>
            ?
           </p>
           <p>
            The Houghton Librarys Emily Dickinson Collection is the largest in the world. It preserves more than 1,000 handwritten autograph poems; some 300 letters; the writing table and chair from her bedroom in Amherst, where she wrote much of her poetry; and the family library, including the poets Bible, and books by the Bronts, the Brownings, George Eliot, Emerson, Shakespeare, and more.
           </p>
          </div>
          <p class="c-content-block__cta">
           <a class="c-block__cta-link a-btn a-btn-secondary a-btn--arrow-right c-content-block__cta-link" href="https://library.harvard.edu/collections/emily-dickinson-collection">
            <span class="a-btn__text">
             Explore the Emily Dickinson Collection
            </span>
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </header>
       </div>
       <div class="b-herosplit__meta-wrap">
        <div class="b-herosplit__meta">
         <span class="b-herosplit__meta-caption">
          [right] Emily Dickinsons writing desk and chair in the Emily Dickinson Room in Houghton Library. Stephanie Mitchell/Harvard Staff Photographer
          <br/>
          [left] Pressed plants from Emily Dickinsons herbarium, 1839-1846 (SEQ. 30).
         </span>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </section>
     <div class="c-block b-spacer all-screens reduce-spacing">
     </div>
     <div class="c-block b-spacer t-theme--light all-screens reduce-spacing">

        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="b-herosplit__media b-herosplit__media-overlay">
        <div class="b-herosplit__figure-secondary c-image--bg c-image--bg-split b-herosplit__figure-secondary--desktop c-image">
         <div aria-label="Vinyl record." class="b-herosplit__img-secondary c-image__image lazyload" data-bgset="https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/34551387326_153ef3b70b_c.jpg 800w 800h" data-expand="200" data-sizes="(min-width: 1260px) 1260px, 100vw" role="img" style="background-image:url('https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/themes/core/assets/img/theme/shims/core-full.png');">
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="b-herosplit__figure c-image--bg c-image--bg-split c-image">
         <div aria-label="Four black and white photographs featuring people and chairs." class="b-herosplit__img c-image__image lazyload" data-bgset="https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/33855826724_203f25c579_h-1152x744.jpg 1152w 744h" data-expand="200" data-sizes="(min-width: 1260px) 1260px, 100vw" role="img" style="background-image:url('https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/themes/core/assets/img/theme/shims/core-full.png');">
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="b-herosplit__content">
        <header class="c-block__content-block c-block__header b-herosplit__content-container c-content-block c-content-block--layout-left">
         <h2 class="c-block__title b-herosplit__title c-content-block__title">
          The Listening Booth
         </h2>
         <div class="c-content-block__content-wrap">
          <div class="c-block__description b-herosplit__description t-sink s-sink c-content-block__content">
           <p>
            The Listening Booth is a digital audio archive featuring a selection of recordings from the Woodberry Poetry Rooms audio visual collection.
           </p>
           <p>
            Listen to poems, lectures, and readings from Ezra Pound, Elizabeth Bishop, W.H. Auden, E.E. Cummings, Jacques Derrida, Sylvia Plath, Robert Frost, Audre Lorde, Anne Carson, Jorge Luis Borges, Anais Nin, Ralph Ellison, Wallace Stevens, Claudia Rankine, Adrienne Rich, T.S. Eliot, and many others.
           </p>
          </div>
          <p class="c-content-block__cta">
           <a class="c-block__cta-link a-btn a-btn-secondary a-btn--arrow-right c-content-block__cta-link" href="https://library.harvard.edu/sites/default/files/static/poetry/listeningbooth/index.html#">
            <span class="a-btn__text">
             Visit the Listening Booth to explore recordings
            </span>
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </header>
       </div>
       <div class="b-herosplit__meta-wrap">
        <div class="b-herosplit__meta">
         <span class="b-herosplit__meta-caption">
          [Right] Harvard Vocarium disc: T. S. Eliot Reading His Poems (1933).  [Left] 1950 Library Journal Photographs of Poetry Room and Lamont Forum Room. Both photographs by Christina Davis, courtesy of the Woodberry Poetry Room, Harvard University.
         </span>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </section>
     <div class="c-block b-spacer t-theme--light all-screens">

     <a name="Eliot">

        <div class="c-block__content-block c-block__header b-media-text__content-container c-content-block c-content-block--layout-left">
         <h2 class="c-block__title b-media-text__title h3 c-content-block__title">
          Provocation series
         </h2>
         <div class="c-content-block__content-wrap">
          <div class="c-block__description b-media-text__text t-sink s-sink c-content-block__content">
           <p>
            As part of the Provocation series, The Woodberry Poetry Room presents poet Cathy Park Hong in conversation with Maggie Nelson (award-winning author of The Argonauts) about Hongs latest work, Minor Feelings: An Asian American Reckoning.
           </p>
          </div>
          <p class="c-content-block__cta">
           <a class="c-block__cta-link a-btn a-btn-secondary a-btn--arrow-right c-content-block__cta-link" href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCx7LgX1FZbs7zguHTxGmPKw">
            <span class="a-btn__text">
             Explore more recordings from the Woodberry Poetry Room on YouTube
            </span>
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </section>

        <div class="c-block__content-block c-block__header b-media-text__content-container c-content-block c-content-block--layout-left">
         <h2 class="c-block__title b-media-text__title h3 c-content-block__title">
          Vocarium Reading series
         </h2>
         <div class="c-content-block__content-wrap">
          <div class="c-block__description b-media-text__text t-sink s-sink c-content-block__content">
           <p>
            The Woodberry Poetry Rooms Vocarium Reading series presents poets M. NourbeSe Philip (author of Zong!) and Cecilia Vicua (author of Spit Temple: The Selected Performances of Cecilia Vicua). This reading is a part of the Poetry Rooms fall 2020 celebration of pioneering women poets from around the world, in commemoration of the centennial of US womens suffrage.
           </p>
          </div>
          <p class="c-content-block__cta">
           <a class="c-block__cta-link a-btn a-btn-secondary a-btn--arrow-right c-content-block__cta-link" href="https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLDtBhamUEttGlNoHGE1seYPjGx6SlReH1">

            </span>

         <figure class="c-image">
          <img alt="Books on a bookshelf." class="c-image__image lazyload" data-expand="200" data-parent-fit="width" data-sizes="(min-width: 1260px) 1260px, 100vw" data-src="https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/AHi_j0104_39-768x576.jpeg" data-srcset="https://www.harvard.edu/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/AHi_j0104_39-375x281.jpeg 375w 281h,

         </figure>

       </div>
       <div class="b-media-text__content">
        <div class="c-block__content-block c-block__header b-media-text__content-container c-content-block c-content-block--layout-left">
         <h2 class="c-block__title b-media-text__title h3 c-content-block__title">
          A public classroom
         </h2>
         <div class="c-content-block__content-wrap">
          <div class="c-block__description b-media-text__text t-sink s-sink c-content-block__content">
           <p>
            Created and directed
            <i>
            </i>
            by
            <i>
            </i>
            Harvard professor Elisa New in partnership with Harvard, Poetry in America is a public television series and multi-platform educational initiative that brings poetry into classrooms and living rooms around the world.
           </p>
           <p>
            Poetry in America offers free online courses for global learners as well as for-credit and professional development courses for undergraduates, graduate students, highly motivated high-school students, and educational practitioners.
           </p>
          </div>
          <p class="c-content-block__cta">
           <a class="c-block__cta-link a-btn a-btn-secondary a-btn--arrow-right c-content-block__cta-link" href="https://www.poetryinamerica.org/">
            <span class="a-btn__text">
             Explore Poetry in America
            </span>
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
